  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer288916559266962174">How do you know whether something is true? How do you convince others to believe the facts? Research shows that the human mind is prone to making thinking errors - predictable mistakes that cause us to believe comfortable lies over inconvenient truths. These errors leave us vulnerable to making decisions based on false beliefs, leading to disastrous consequences for our pe</span>
  <span id="freeText288916559266962174" style="display:none">How do you know whether something is true? How do you convince others to believe the facts? Research shows that the human mind is prone to making thinking errors - predictable mistakes that cause us to believe comfortable lies over inconvenient truths. These errors leave us vulnerable to making decisions based on false beliefs, leading to disastrous consequences for our personal lives, relationships, careers, civic and political engagement, and for our society as a whole.<br /><br />Fortunately, cognitive and behavioral scientists have uncovered many useful strategies for overcoming our mental flaws. This book presents a variety of research-based tools for ensuring that our beliefs are aligned with reality. With examples from daily life and an engaging style, the book will provide you with the skills to avoid thinking errors and help others to do so, preventing disasters and facilitating success for yourself, those you care about, and our society.</span>
  <a data-text-id="288916559266962174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1278344-does-this-book-focus-on-helping-you-to">Does this book focus on helping you to make political arguments (to sway others to your view)? Or does it provide questions and tools to help you to strengthen critical thinking skills when consuming media? Is there a narrow political agenda here, or could the skills be applied broadly? Would the book deeply offend conservatives or liberals?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1278344'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F36647568-the-truth-seeker-s-handbook">like</a></span>

</li>

</li>

</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/39319380-gleb-tsipursky"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1547175721i/39319380._UX100_CR0,6,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/39319380-gleb-tsipursky">Gleb Tsipursky</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It first provides you with critical thinking skills to see reality clearly. Then, it discusses how to sway others to a point of view aligned with real<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It first provides you with critical thinking skills to see reality clearly. Then, it discusses how to sway others to a point of view aligned with reality. The techniques for swaying others described in this book would not work if they are used to try to persuade people to a viewpoint that's not aligned with reality. <br /><br />The skills are process skills, not agenda-based: anyone could apply them, of any political orientation. <br /><br />The book has been praised by conservatives and liberals alike. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2207198259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2207198259" />
    <a title="Niklas Pivic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2106358-niklas-pivic"><img alt="Niklas Pivic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556808424p2/2106358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2207198259?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niklas Pivic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niklas Pivic" href="/user/show/2106358-niklas-pivic">Niklas Pivic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2106358-niklas-pivic?shelf=anger">anger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2106358-niklas-pivic?shelf=bureaucracy">bureaucracy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2106358-niklas-pivic?shelf=usa">usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2106358-niklas-pivic?shelf=bullshit">bullshit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2106358-niklas-pivic?shelf=christianity">christianity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2106358-niklas-pivic?shelf=annotated">annotated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2106358-niklas-pivic?shelf=insanity">insanity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2106358-niklas-pivic?shelf=criticism">criticism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2106358-niklas-pivic?shelf=1900s">1900s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2106358-niklas-pivic?shelf=analysis">analysis</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2207198259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15126953839439211751">I'll say this is a very American book, at its core; the stock images that cover the top of every chapter repelled me, as did the bad formatting of the book. Reading it made me realise two main issues: a) it badly needed editing, mainly due to its style and b) it would benefit from a complete overhaul where it comes to language. Where persons like Noam Chomsky and Naomi Klein can navigate the oft-muddled waters where they run the risk of losing a reader completely but somehow manage to stay stead</span>
  <span id="freeText15126953839439211751" style="display:none">I'll say this is a very American book, at its core; the stock images that cover the top of every chapter repelled me, as did the bad formatting of the book. Reading it made me realise two main issues: a) it badly needed editing, mainly due to its style and b) it would benefit from a complete overhaul where it comes to language. Where persons like Noam Chomsky and Naomi Klein can navigate the oft-muddled waters where they run the risk of losing a reader completely but somehow manage to stay steadfast through harsh waters, the author—regardless of his best intentions—made me skip reading a lot of the time.<br /><br />Also, on the Kindle edition of this book: the entire book contains a slew of hyperlinked sections of words. As such, the book is near-impossible to check when using a Kindle reader, partly because how bad the built-in web browser is, and partly because it's impossible to read the link sources when offline.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15126953839439211751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2193167877" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2193167877" />
    <a title="L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4847028-l"><img alt="L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302916636p2/4847028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2193167877?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L" href="/user/show/4847028-l">L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4847028-l?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4847028-l?shelf=psychology">psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4847028-l?shelf=political">political</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193167877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14059536024785459750">We all imagine that our beliefs, decisions, and actions are based on a sound foundation. Unfortunately, that rosy opinion of ourselves is often false. Our own brains have a tendency to take convenient shortcuts, such as "gut reactions" and a reliance of "cognitive biases" that lead us astray. <br/><br/>Shortcuts save time and energy - that's why we use them - but occasionally they create personal or societal disasters. If we could only remember to search for the truth before major decisions, we'd all be b</span>
  <span id="freeText14059536024785459750" style="display:none">We all imagine that our beliefs, decisions, and actions are based on a sound foundation. Unfortunately, that rosy opinion of ourselves is often false. Our own brains have a tendency to take convenient shortcuts, such as "gut reactions" and a reliance of "cognitive biases" that lead us astray. <br /><br />Shortcuts save time and energy - that's why we use them - but occasionally they create personal or societal disasters. If we could only remember to search for the truth before major decisions, we'd all be better off. Dr. Gleb Tsipursky has written a wonderful book to help us cut through misinformation, emotional traps, and hone in on the truth. <br /><br />I found lots of practical information, stuff that we might (or might not) learn through the hard knocks of life. The "Individual Truth-Seeking" section was my favorite part of the book. I've figured out some of this on my own, but if such a clear presentation had been available a couple of decades ago, the road would have been smoother and I'd be a happier person. <br /><br />The second section, "Truth-Seeking &amp; Other People" is also useful. I plan to study this material and try to use it habitually. I am strongly drawn to Chapter 28 "Collaborative Truth-Seeking" and Chapter 29 "Having Trouble Resolving Disagreements? Here Are Some Effective Techniques." <br /><br />I'm a bit burned out politically, so the final section "Truth Seeking &amp; Civic Life" was less enjoyable for me. But that says more about me than Dr. Tsipursky's writing. It doesn't matter if we are Liberal or Independent or Conservative. It's important that politicians base their policies on real facts and rational thinking. We voters must recognize (and resist) when politicians are trying to manipulate us through our biases and emotions. And above all, we must recognize good journalism and avoid being fooled by fake news. <br /><br />Again, our political viewpoints aren't nearly as important as HOW we arrive there. The third section of this book helps a lot. <br /><br />Finally, unlike a lot of "non-fiction" books on the market, this one is meticulously researched and referenced. Buy the e-book version and you will find links to every claim made. Look up the hard facts and scientific research for yourself. You should expect no less from book about Truth. Gleb Tsipursky delivers his premise and backs it up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14059536024785459750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer6537729474162641135">This is a remarkable book. A few of the images in it give away some left-leaning political bias, but the chapters full of general principles and the specific debate tactics used successfully by the author are extraordinarily valuable to anyone with a point of view they want to verify and defend.   <span id="freeText6537729474162641135" style="display:none">This is a remarkable book. A few of the images in it give away some left-leaning political bias, but the chapters full of general principles and the specific debate tactics used successfully by the author are extraordinarily valuable to anyone with a point of view they want to verify and defend. And there are ample portions devoted to difficulties and imperfections on both sides of the current divide. You do not have to be a statistician or a psychologist to grasp the explanations of probabilistic thinking or "lizard brain" and "elephant" analogies. I recommend it. </span>

  <span id="freeText133272077829331691" style="display:none">Very Effective and Realistic book! <br />Thank you very much Dr. Gleb Tsipursky for publishing “The Truth-Seeker’s Handbook” book which will really help people to develop more realistic expectations and accurate beliefs, which are necessary for achieving goals. I will definitely use the strategy included in this book to defend myself from the Attentional bias in the future. Thanks again for making my career path beautiful and I feel very grateful to read this book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10115898843569056386">Dr. Gleb Tsipursky has written a timely and essential book for all who are fed up with the current post- truth times we live in and are looking for ways to put real, verifiable truth back into public discourse. Using easy to follow scientific methods and data Dr. Tsipursky demonstrates how to make all our interactions more meaningful when we rely on verifiable, fact-based truth rather than emotionally charged rhetoric, ensuring that our beliefs are aligned with reality. He gives examples of how </span>
  <span id="freeText10115898843569056386" style="display:none">Dr. Gleb Tsipursky has written a timely and essential book for all who are fed up with the current post- truth times we live in and are looking for ways to put real, verifiable truth back into public discourse. Using easy to follow scientific methods and data Dr. Tsipursky demonstrates how to make all our interactions more meaningful when we rely on verifiable, fact-based truth rather than emotionally charged rhetoric, ensuring that our beliefs are aligned with reality. He gives examples of how to recognize false information and how to help others do the same in a non-contentious, rational manner. Well worth your time to read and share with others. Highly recommended</span>

<div id="review_3323774134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3323774134" />
    <a title="Tasnuva Tonny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104940579-tasnuva-tonny"><img alt="Tasnuva Tonny" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3323774134?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tasnuva Tonny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tasnuva Tonny" href="/user/show/104940579-tasnuva-tonny">Tasnuva Tonny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3323774134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16476794107562214136">I would like to give my heartfelt thanks to Dr. Tsipursky to launch such a thoughtful book as the book has been organized into three sections. The first outlines truth-seeking strategies pursued primarily for the sake of avoiding false beliefs within ourselves. The second deals with truth-seeking in relation to other people. Finally, the third describes two strategies for individuals, teams, and organizations to see the truth and thus make better decisions. The effort I put into truth-seeking wi</span>
  <span id="freeText16476794107562214136" style="display:none">I would like to give my heartfelt thanks to Dr. Tsipursky to launch such a thoughtful book as the book has been organized into three sections. The first outlines truth-seeking strategies pursued primarily for the sake of avoiding false beliefs within ourselves. The second deals with truth-seeking in relation to other people. Finally, the third describes two strategies for individuals, teams, and organizations to see the truth and thus make better decisions. The effort I put into truth-seeking will be very much worth it. This book is quite helpful as this book includes more resources on effective decision-making. This book provides the manual for truth-seeking skills.<br />This book would have been helpful in the past as I just came to know about how our minds work, we can be intentional about influencing our own thinking and feeling patterns. We can evaluate reality more clearly, make better decisions, and improve our ability to achieve goals. Once I had to go through fundamental attribution error which is also called correspondence bias in my university life. One of my best friend had a relationship with a bad guy. I was trying to make her understand that she is going to wrong path but my other friends found me wrong as they didn’t even know about my that friend who was involved with a bad guy. Without knowing the proper reason they all were misunderstanding me. If I would get chance to read this book earlier, I might solve this correspondence bias by applying different debiasing strategies as described in this book. <br />What I read proved surprising and unexpected to know about the Cognitive biases - that lead us to make poor decisions, such as overconfidence effect, optimism bias, and planning fallacy. I agree with the author that our bad decision-making comes from failing to understand the role of emotions in making decisions. These bad decisions are costly. In our everyday life, bad decisions cause us to lose money, time, relationships, health, and happiness. Making bad decisions in the workplace results in our organizations losing money, time, and reputation, as well as undermining teamwork and employee morale. Now which I will be taking forward with me is I can make the best decisions possible for myself my team and my organization.<br />I think Mere-exposure effect might be vulnerable. It refers to our brain’s tendency to believe something is true and good just because we are familiar with it, regardless of whether that something is actually true and good. Often I have been criticized by few people because in spite of being a girl I have chosen Textile Engineering as they think men prefer this subject rather than women but I truly feel that I enjoyed 4 years of my academic life. Also I did MBA in the same field. Everything in our lives, personal and professional, results from our decisions. Making good decisions depends on us having the right information. Practicing the skills of truth-seeking will help us develop more realistic expectations and accurate beliefs, which are necessary.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16476794107562214136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laszlo Makay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laszlo Makay" href="/user/show/34852089-laszlo-makay">Laszlo Makay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2203556518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7367228389051382947">There are various types of books around: fictions with great characters, comics with beautiful pictures and textbooks of great academic knowledge. Each has its aim and target audience. Gleb Tsipursky’s book is for those who would like to see clearly. <br/><br/>Do you feel that sometimes you are just lost among the flood of opinionated statements from businessman, religious leaders and politicians? Do you feel disoriented when targeted messages and advertisements are bombarding you from all angles? Do you </span>
  <span id="freeText7367228389051382947" style="display:none">There are various types of books around: fictions with great characters, comics with beautiful pictures and textbooks of great academic knowledge. Each has its aim and target audience. Gleb Tsipursky’s book is for those who would like to see clearly. <br /><br />Do you feel that sometimes you are just lost among the flood of opinionated statements from businessman, religious leaders and politicians? Do you feel disoriented when targeted messages and advertisements are bombarding you from all angles? Do you feel annoyed reading never-ending facebook debates with parties whose slogan surely is „Never really listen”?<br /><br />I do feel all these sometimes. And I think that I am not alone. It is because of the nature of the modern media, including the distracting social one and because we have limited time to uncover reliable sources of information. Occasionally we also have limited motivation to face the truth (instead of believing in convenient falsehoods).<br /><br />However, if we look around we can see that successful people are not behaving like that. They don’t believe in whatever is said to them. They don’t let themselves misled and deceived, not even by themselves. They seek out the necessary facts to make fruitful decisions, serving their own best interest, not that of others. They learn the effective methods to perform these tasks, essential for success.<br /><br />This book is about this truth-seeking process, describing its problems and difficulties, revealing the consequences of its failure and providing valuable advices to make it more effective. So this book is for those who has aims and who would like to maximize their chances to reach them.<br />The book contains a lot of chapters about various topics, each supported by relevant scientific research. You don’t have to follow all of the advices. As said above we all have limited time to read and learn. If you have an aim or passion you can focus on the relevant topics/chapters and learn only those bit of information which are critical to you. Take the title seriously and use the book as it is: a handbook of practical advices regarding modern age problems.<br /></span>

    <a title="Kezia Tabago" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104818863-kezia-tabago"><img alt="Kezia Tabago" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3324679485?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kezia Tabago" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kezia Tabago" href="/user/show/104818863-kezia-tabago">Kezia Tabago</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3324679485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12172316347945808388">All I can say is: I cannot put this book down!<br/><br/>This book proves that we can be c-suite executives and still be blind about fundamentals. This book comes to the rescue when it comes to dissonance in teams, miscommunication, lapses in decision making and business failures. There is much to know about business decisions and rational thinking given so many potholes, however, this material keeps us in check. Points raised in this book serve as backbone to questions we may have in the internet of thing</span>
  <span id="freeText12172316347945808388" style="display:none">All I can say is: I cannot put this book down!<br /><br />This book proves that we can be c-suite executives and still be blind about fundamentals. This book comes to the rescue when it comes to dissonance in teams, miscommunication, lapses in decision making and business failures. There is much to know about business decisions and rational thinking given so many potholes, however, this material keeps us in check. Points raised in this book serve as backbone to questions we may have in the internet of things. A key take-away here that could’ve served a big part in my decisions was making them and choosing the best option after a thorough evaluation using probabilistic thinking and multi-attribute utility. I am guilty of various biases because most aspects are related to emotions, thus making me blind-sided to many areas. It surprised me that Dr. Tsipursky has a special portion in his journal about mistakes and learning and his story about the computation about purchasing a home. It just goes to show that people need to take a step back and create a system for decisions, personal or business. If there’s one thing that helps improve decision making processes, it is having to make decisions based on choices associated to numerical values. It is difficult enough to put a handle on non-monetary considerations, and the pointers in this book addressed that issue through a solid example. Another key take-away from this book is attentional bias. When I first started working, I tend to make rash decisions (again, I was guilty of another bias – overconfidence bias) and I spent little evaluation on different possibilities. It made me sort of reminiscent and it made me remember t always take into consideration all possible options and outcomes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12172316347945808388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText16972530117811561006" style="display:none">The seven steps for avoiding disastrous decisions is one of the best lessons for me to take my decision in a right way. And also ranking between the choices and differentiate them by giving them numbers will help me to find the best alternative. On that situation I read this book and I was able to rank my choices and find the best alternative. I made the ranking and found that my current city stands out and was the best choice for me.<br /><br />The ranking system really surprised me and I’ve learned that we can rank between our choices and find out the best choice by giving them different ranks. I’ll definitely take this lesson and will apply it to my future operation.<br /><br />I think I am vulnerable to planning fallacy bias. Sometimes I feel that everything is going to go according to plan, I don’t pay nearly enough attention to potential problems and fail to account for them in my plans. From now I’ll anticipate the kind of problems that might come up in advance and decide the strategies I am going to use to address them. And I’ll reserve quite a lot of resources, of time, money, social capital, whatever relevant to the project to address the planning fallacy, to address the planning fallacy, to address unanticipated threats, as well as to address unanticipated opportunities, that I don’t want to miss out.</span>

<div id="review_3252738363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3252738363" />
    <a title="Ruona Sargin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/105185096-ruona-sargin"><img alt="Ruona Sargin" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3252738363?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruona Sargin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruona Sargin" href="/user/show/105185096-ruona-sargin">Ruona Sargin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3252738363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1507020334262890812">Basically, I love to fact check what anyone conveys to be the "Truth". The spread of fake news is so alarming these days. Hence, when I saw this book entitled, Truth-Seeker's Handbook, it was a mystery at first. But will definitely be a guide for anyone who desires to know the truth at all times. This book proved me wrong in my choices of being too positive to a point that I forgot about optimism bias. Every aspiring leader and researcher needs to read this book.<br/><br/>My favorite part of this book is </span>
  <span id="freeText1507020334262890812" style="display:none">Basically, I love to fact check what anyone conveys to be the "Truth". The spread of fake news is so alarming these days. Hence, when I saw this book entitled, Truth-Seeker's Handbook, it was a mystery at first. But will definitely be a guide for anyone who desires to know the truth at all times. This book proved me wrong in my choices of being too positive to a point that I forgot about optimism bias. Every aspiring leader and researcher needs to read this book.<br /><br />My favorite part of this book is on Chapter 8 -Avoiding Professional Disasters With Behavioral Science. If only I read this book earlier, I wouldn't have made poor choices in hiring some members of my team who I previously worked with. I was so confident in their boldness to handle a task and expected so much from them. But somehow, they were just "talkers" and ended up as liabilities.<br /><br />It is true that researchers have found that our brains make systematic and predictable errors - what behavioral scientists call cognitive biases -that lead us to make poor decisions, such as overconfidence effect, optimism bias, and planning fallacy. Optimism Bias - Overconfidence feeds into another thinking error, optimism bias, which refers to us being excessively optimistic about the future. Studies show we tend to believe our risk of suffering negative events is less than it actually is and we overestimate the likelihood of positive events. We fall into optimism bias frequently in the workplace and overemphasizing the benefits of projects and understating the costs.<br /><br />I learned about the optimism bias and I am a victim of the overconfidence effect. I will have to implement the strategies stated in this book. It will help me make better decisions in the future.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3244394167" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3244394167?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrice Sargin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrice Sargin" href="/user/show/104956493-beatrice-sargin">Beatrice Sargin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3244394167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5330766872757317665">The book, "The Truth-Seeker's Handbook is amazing!<br/><br/>I have always been a lover of the truth, no matter what. The title of the book captured my attention to read its content and I have no regret. For me, there can only be one "truth" and it can be acquired through knowledge. Truth is wonderful. Learning about ways to achieve the truth and be a better version yourself is my goal. I definitely recommend this book.<br/><br/>If I had read this book earlier, I wouldn't have felt so much anger with my superior in </span>
  <span id="freeText5330766872757317665" style="display:none">The book, "The Truth-Seeker's Handbook is amazing!<br /><br />I have always been a lover of the truth, no matter what. The title of the book captured my attention to read its content and I have no regret. For me, there can only be one "truth" and it can be acquired through knowledge. Truth is wonderful. Learning about ways to achieve the truth and be a better version yourself is my goal. I definitely recommend this book.<br /><br />If I had read this book earlier, I wouldn't have felt so much anger with my superior in the company I previously worked with. I would have known that his behavior was a result of "confirmation bias". Hence, I would have acted differently and not being rude nor bitter with the way he handled work delegations. I would have been patient and learn to listen to him to accept changes. But since I knew his nature, I just wouldn't listen to him at all. I saw that he had no truth in him and can't teach me anything.<br /><br />In this book, I read about "Confirmation Bias". At the extreme, confirmation bias turns into wishful thinking. Our beliefs stem from what we want to believe, instead of what is true. Confirmation bias is a big part of the polarization in my opinion, especially in politics and among others.<br /><br />I am truly vulnerable to confirmation bias. To deal with it, I have to employ the flip-floppers strategy. It helps to practice mentally associating positive emotions such as pride and excitement, with the decision to change our minds and update our beliefs based on new evidence. I feel proud to be a flip-flopper!<br /><br />In addition to associating positive emotions with changing our minds, I have learned to use these habits to develop more accurate beliefs:<br />1) Deliberately seek out contradictory evidence to my opinion on a topic and praise myself after giving that evidence a fair consideration.<br />2) Consider the best possible form of arguments against my position and be open to consider someone's arguments.<br />3) Focus on updating my beliefs on controversial and emotional topics as these are harder for human mind to manage well.<br /><br />These ideas from the book will help me a lot as I intend to seek the truth always!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5330766872757317665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I agree with the context stated about how our mind works and what does the autopilot and intentional system do. It also explains how our gut-based ways could lead to disastrous decision. <br/>What I like about this book is it explains how our instincts could control us resulting to terrible decisions.   <span id="freeText13258470506013418156" style="display:none">Reading this book is very helpful to me. I agree with the context stated about how our mind works and what does the autopilot and intentional system do. It also explains how our gut-based ways could lead to disastrous decision. <br />What I like about this book is it explains how our instincts could control us resulting to terrible decisions. I could still remember one situation in my life where I somehow regretted because I follow my gut without evaluating my decision thoroughly. I chose my college course based on what I know is easy and because of the opinion of everyone else. I knew from the very start before I graduated in High School that I wanted to be a soldier just like my father, but my family and friends kept telling me that I should not. The training is so hard and I might die sooner. So, I take other path, that is completely different from I really love to do. Now, there's no more enough time to do what I like, there's so much time and resources wasted. If I read this book long time ago, I might not feel any regret now because this will guide me on how to make better decision in my life. <br />By reading this book, I learned so many things. Like in our modern time, many people go with their gut because it feels comfortable even if this will lead to bad decision. I usually follow my gut in making decisions in so many areas of my life, and ended up with regret. I've learned that we should verify our gut first, whether it could be a threat or opportunity, one will surely take this passage with me moving forward. I’m a person who decides abruptly without thinking the result as long as it produces good result. I usually don’t think of the long-term effect, like buying things that are not useful and are not worth buying but could satisfy me in a short period of time. I will definitely follow the intentional system instead of the autopilot. The intentional system changes my automatic thinking, feeling, and behavioral patterns to avoid dangerous judgment errors.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1862221240690477922">During this time, the issue of COVID-19 is a worldwide concern. The advice to stay at home to prevent the spread of the virus is a must. Hence, what better way to stay productive even at home is to learn something new? So I came across reading the book entitled, “The Truth Seeker’s Handbook: A Science Based Guide”. The title got me curious and as I look at the table of contents for the topics and it’s really interesting. <br/><br/>Sometimes, it’s odd that we are eager to know the truth but most of the tim</span>
  <span id="freeText1862221240690477922" style="display:none">During this time, the issue of COVID-19 is a worldwide concern. The advice to stay at home to prevent the spread of the virus is a must. Hence, what better way to stay productive even at home is to learn something new? So I came across reading the book entitled, “The Truth Seeker’s Handbook: A Science Based Guide”. The title got me curious and as I look at the table of contents for the topics and it’s really interesting. <br /><br />Sometimes, it’s odd that we are eager to know the truth but most of the time when it’s delivered to us we can’t handle it. When facing facts, we deal with negative emotions in which our minds are in denial and we go back to the things we believe in. I am guilty of this as most of the time my thinking is irrational when facing the hard truth. I am glad that this book focused on how we make decisions, on dealing our emotions and being rational. I am quoting the author on this, “Sticking to pre-existing beliefs that do not align with reality causes us to develop unrealistic expectations” and this has given me a new perspective on how I should deal with my emotions rationally. As what the author has said, “the emotional payoff is just one part you gain in orienting toward inconvenient truths instead of comfortable falsehoods”. By saying so, this will prevent us from making bad decisions which may have greater cost in our lives.<br /><br />This book has also identified different biases and presented strategies through real life experiences in which, as a reader, I can relate to. It speaks volume as it can be easily understood and reflect on your own if you have been suffering from any biases. I also love how the topics are presented like the first 2 sections of the book which focuses on individual aspects and how you can learn and grow and the last section talks more about leadership and the organization. I will definitely recommend this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1862221240690477922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

This handbook changes everything. I always thought I was pretty good at making decisions until I realized what a rookie I am.<br/><br/>I was really surprised by how much this book helped me in my daily life seeking for truth. I consider The Truth-Seeker’s Handbook: A Science-Based Guide to be the best book I had ever read. Since I graduated college, I was faced with making important life </span>
  <span id="freeText1325529789198285054" style="display:none">I just finished reading The Truth-Seeker’s Handbook: A Science-Based Guide. I can't express through words what I feel. This handbook changes everything. I always thought I was pretty good at making decisions until I realized what a rookie I am.<br /><br />I was really surprised by how much this book helped me in my daily life seeking for truth. I consider The Truth-Seeker’s Handbook: A Science-Based Guide to be the best book I had ever read. Since I graduated college, I was faced with making important life decisions. Unfortunately, I made very few smart decisions. As I look back, I definitely could have changed it all with the help of this book.<br /><br />The "Strategies for Individual and Organizational Decision-Making" section was my favorite part of the book. Where it provides “Guidelines on Avoiding Disastrous Decisions”, it really helped me in making some big decisions in life. This book does a great job at making you look at your decisions from an objective viewpoint.<br /><br />I think I am more vulnerable to planning fallacy. I always have the tendency to underestimate the amount of time a project will take to complete. After reading this book I learned that I need to think about how long I usually have taken in the past to complete a project and break it down into smaller parts and consider how long each part will take. I would definitely recommend this book to anyone, especially people that have many big decisions ahead of them in the near future.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2193565707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2193565707" />
    <a title="Søren Ekelund" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74170544-s-ren-ekelund"><img alt="Søren Ekelund" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513522255p2/74170544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2193565707?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Søren Ekelund" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Søren Ekelund" href="/user/show/74170544-s-ren-ekelund">Søren Ekelund</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193565707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13936193706822763749">The Truth Seekers Handbook is a collection of articles written and collected by Gleb Tsipursky.<br/><br/>It introduces the reader to the various biases modern people may suffer from, keeping them from accurately perceiving the truth, as well as the tools to overcome them.<br/><br/>The methods are based in science and well documented, and the author gives examples of use as well as anecdotes from his own experiences while explaining how they work.<br/><br/>Gleb also uses real world situations when pointing out the different b</span>
  <span id="freeText13936193706822763749" style="display:none">The Truth Seekers Handbook is a collection of articles written and collected by Gleb Tsipursky.<br /><br />It introduces the reader to the various biases modern people may suffer from, keeping them from accurately perceiving the truth, as well as the tools to overcome them.<br /><br />The methods are based in science and well documented, and the author gives examples of use as well as anecdotes from his own experiences while explaining how they work.<br /><br />Gleb also uses real world situations when pointing out the different biases and obstacles to truth in modern life, but commendably stays as neutral as humanely possible when it comes to the political scene.<br /><br />He ends the book with a “call to arms” against lies, alternate facts and fake news, in the form of the Pro-Truth Pledge, a grass root movement to further truth in politics, and keep politicians and public figures honest, something that strikes me as a useful, and seriously needed, measure in the current political climate.<br /><br />I found the book to be an interesting read, and though I pride myself on some insight in both the human psyche and fact seeking in general, I still found several new tools.<br /><br />I recommend reading the book from start to finish, and then use it as reference, when the need arises. This is an easy task, since the chapters are in article form and each deals with a separate term or tool.<br /><br />All in all I really recommend this book to anyone seeking a bit more clarity in their everyday lives, while navigating fellows, news and politics.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13936193706822763749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15821305617711136804">This is one of the books that I am excited to read until the last chapter because you would learn so many things. There are numerous strategies and techniques that one can apply to avoid potential disasters in decision making. <br/>I agreed with one of the statements in the book about Truth-seeking is a journey, not a destination. I am an introvert person. I usually follow my gut when deciding things for myself that led to dangerous errors. But, when I read the book, I've learned that you need to hav</span>
  <span id="freeText15821305617711136804" style="display:none">This is one of the books that I am excited to read until the last chapter because you would learn so many things. There are numerous strategies and techniques that one can apply to avoid potential disasters in decision making. <br />I agreed with one of the statements in the book about Truth-seeking is a journey, not a destination. I am an introvert person. I usually follow my gut when deciding things for myself that led to dangerous errors. But, when I read the book, I've learned that you need to have research first instead of becoming impulsive, gut is helpful, but it can also lead us to a wrongful way.<br />One of the situations in the past that I made a wrong decision was when I applied for employment to a car company. I just applied because I saw their hiring post online and because the location was convenient to me. This without thinking what could be my future when I join the organization. I got hired but I only lasted for 3 months because of the poor people management and super toxic culture.<br />If I read this book back then, I should have done my thorough research about their profile, what benefits they have for their employees, and would not end up applying and wasting my time there. But I feel good reading this book as it serves as my guide in making decisions every day.<br />This book helps me every time I go out for shopping. Before, I just get what I want even if I don't need it as long as it looks beautiful in my eyes and ended up just using it once or twice. After reading this book, my behavior changes drastically when it comes to managing my finances. Now, I have an expense tracker. I also think many times and do my research if this product is worth buying. I’m still tempted to buy the latest products in the store but at the back of my mind I can hear - "Hey, get yourself a reward, buy that one, you only live once, so enjoy your money". However, I remember the 8-Step Decision-Making Model stated in this book that greatly help in avoiding serious problems.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11806429531349065187">Read this on Kindle. I love the concept of this book but the execution was clumsy. The memes were not cleanly executed and looked a bit off.   <span id="freeText11806429531349065187" style="display:none">Read this on Kindle. I love the concept of this book but the execution was clumsy. The memes were not cleanly executed and looked a bit off. They were less the common definition of memes and more just smart advice on stock photos. <br /><br />There were a few typos and formatting errors. Also, Chapter 52 and 53, despite having different titles, have nearly identical text. <br /><br />The positives:<br /><br />I enjoyed most the chapters that applied EGRIP (Emotions, Goals, Rapport, Information, Positive Reinforcement.) EGRIP is a technique for getting someone of a different opinion to meet you in the common ground of facts. <br /><br />Unfortunately, the EGRIP chapters dealt with Trump stupidities long out of the news. Since Trump produces idiocy rapidly, such chapters felt old. Those topics are better suited for a blog post. <br /><br />Still, this book fills a need. We can all use a reminder that our emotions steer us away from facts. <br /><br />The book seems rushed. With a clean, user-friendly, share-ready presentation, the ideas could have a positive impact on our information-heavy culture. <br /><br />Larry Nocella<br />Author of the novel, Razor Wire Karma, available on Amazon</span>
  <a data-text-id="11806429531349065187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3459390520" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3459390520" />
    <a title="Precious Quinte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/115307412-precious-quinte"><img alt="Precious Quinte" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3459390520?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Precious Quinte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Precious Quinte" href="/user/show/115307412-precious-quinte">Precious Quinte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3459390520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9062150705971926843">I am grateful to have read this book because it has given me enlightenment on how our decisions are greatly affected by people's opinions and suggestions on things. This book also has provided me with various strategies on how to be a good decision-maker.<br/><br/>I never thought that I could relate in this book especially in Chapter 9: Stop! Live the Life You Want. I could still remember how my godfather convinced me to enroll Accountancy as my college course because he told me that you will earn a lot a</span>
  <span id="freeText9062150705971926843" style="display:none">I am grateful to have read this book because it has given me enlightenment on how our decisions are greatly affected by people's opinions and suggestions on things. This book also has provided me with various strategies on how to be a good decision-maker.<br /><br />I never thought that I could relate in this book especially in Chapter 9: Stop! Live the Life You Want. I could still remember how my godfather convinced me to enroll Accountancy as my college course because he told me that you will earn a lot and you can easily land a job right after you graduate in college and all other good things you can think of relating to accountancy. Being so young ( a girl who was only 14 that finished high school and completely has no idea how the world works) and desperate to help my family right after graduation I believed him because I thought he knows better than I do and helping my family immediately is the only thing that I have on my mind at that moment. After taking the first semester of that course, I felt like I wasn't really happy, it doesn't excite me or sparked even a tiny interest in me.<br />I began to ask myself, is this course really for me? Do I see myself doing this kind of job until I get old? My heart and mind said no, that's when I realized that I have to shift or else I will be stuck with a course that was chosen based on my godfather's opinion.<br /><br />I was really surprised that there's a specific term to this kind situation, the mere- exposure effect where our brain has a tendency of believing that something is good and true just because it is somehow common for us.<br /><br />I learned about many types of biases especially the optimism bias which I really admit that I am a willing victim of this kind of bias. I always think that everything will go well and nothing can go wrong when I am deciding on things. But it turned out that I was completely wrong and too much of a good thing is not good anymore. Anything can happen, it may be good or bad that's why I am trying my best to address this bias with the help of this book. Had I read this book before, I might not be able to experience this kind of situation but still, I am grateful to have read this book especially in this time of the pandemic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9062150705971926843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary Monti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary Monti" href="/user/show/74269515-gary-monti">Gary Monti</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2196059529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1278360878667547825">If you are looking to step away from all the confusion with fake news and find a place to stand grounded in facts this book is a "must." It is, IMO, a foundational book that is a great reference for determining where to begin when building a comprehensive, focused approach to assessing one's own approach to facts and opinions as well as examining statements/claims made by others. The breadth of concepts covered is good. The one shortcoming I found is an occasional lack of connectivity or flow in</span>
  <span id="freeText1278360878667547825" style="display:none">If you are looking to step away from all the confusion with fake news and find a place to stand grounded in facts this book is a "must." It is, IMO, a foundational book that is a great reference for determining where to begin when building a comprehensive, focused approach to assessing one's own approach to facts and opinions as well as examining statements/claims made by others. The breadth of concepts covered is good. The one shortcoming I found is an occasional lack of connectivity or flow in some of the presentations, e.g., some of the questions asked at the end of a chapter. It's important to emphasize, though, I view this as very minor. The book is a keeper.<br />A companion book to consider is Jay Henrichs, "Thank You For Arguing," which dives directly into rhetorical flaws often used to disseminate illogical, misleading arguments.</span>

This book is very helpful as it provides resources on effective decision-making. <br /><br />As a businesswoman, I find it hard to make decisions.   <span id="freeText14551314428509126190" style="display:none">The Truth-Seeker's Handbook definitely comes handy for me. I may not be a big time businessman but I was able to learn a lot from the solutions being presented in this handbook, especially in the area of leadership and decision making. These 2 are vital for any businesses - big or small. <br /><br />As an owner of a small enterprise, I struggle to make small decision every single day. Whether it's how to deal with tardiness to promoting an employee, everything has to be in place and carefully thought of. The handbook has provided a factual, experience-based and scientific approach to every day issues. <br /><br />This is a worthwhile read. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14551314428509126190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14589400266536130081"><strong>Truth and how to find it</strong><br/><br/>This book gives a lot of insight into how our brains work and helps us tell truth from untruth. It was very insightful in how to keep ourselves from falling into the pit of falsehoods that seems to surround us every day. It did seem a bit repetitive from time to time but otherwise a very helpful tool.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''

    }
  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_18304'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18304.The_Anti_Christ?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Anti-Christ<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/1938.Friedrich_Nietzsche?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Friedrich Nietzsche<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.92 avg rating &mdash; 20,982 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1895\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer3703842858635510867\">The reference to the Antichrist is not intended to refer to the biblical Antichrist but is rather an attack on the \"slave morality\" and apathy of Western Christianity. Nietzsche\'s basic claim is that Christianity is a poisoner of western culture and <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3703842858635510867\" style=\"display:none\">The reference to the Antichrist is not intended to refer to the biblical Antichrist but is rather an attack on the &quot;slave morality&quot; and apathy of Western Christianity. Nietzsche\'s basic claim is that Christianity is a poisoner of western culture and perversion of the words of and practice of Jesus. Throughout the text, Nietzsche is very critical of institutionalized religion and its priest class, from which he himself was descended. The majority of the book is a systematic attack upon the interpretations of Christ\'s words by St. Paul and those who followed him. Nietzsche claimed in the Foreword to have written the book for a very limited readership. In order to understand the book, he asserted that the reader &quot;... must be honest in intellectual matters to the point of hardness to so much as endure my seriousness, my passion.&quot; The reader should be above politics and nationalism. Also, the usefulness or harmfulness of truth should not be a concern. Characteristics such as &quot;Strength which prefers questions for which no one today is sufficiently daring; courage for the forbidden&quot; are also needed. He disdained all other readers.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"3703842858635510867\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/225112.The_Global_Village"><img alt="The Global Village: Transformations in World Life and Media in the 21st Century" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1348970646l/225112._SX98_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_225112'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/225112.The_Global_Village?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Global Village: Transformations in World Life and Media in the 21st Century<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/455.Marshall_McLuhan?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Marshall McLuhan<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.14 avg rating &mdash; 229 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1989\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer3463483825302577122\">Extending the visionary early work of the late Marshall McLuhan, The Global Village, one of his last collaborative efforts, applies that vision to today\'s worldwide, integrated electronic network. When McLuhan\'s groundbreaking Understanding Media was<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3463483825302577122\" style=\"display:none\">Extending the visionary early work of the late Marshall McLuhan, The Global Village, one of his last collaborative efforts, applies that vision to today\'s worldwide, integrated electronic network. When McLuhan\'s groundbreaking Understanding Media was published in 1964, the media as we know it today did not exist. But McLuhan\'s argument, that the technological extensions of human consciousness were racing ahead of our ability to understand their consequences, has never been more compelling. And if the medium is the message, as McLuhan maintained, then the message is becoming almost impossible to decipher. In The Global Village, McLuhan and co-author Bruce R. Powers propose a detailed conceptual framework in terms of which the technological advances of the past two decades may be understood. At the heart of their theory is the argument that today\'s users of technology are caught between two very different ways of perceiving the world. On the one hand there is what they refer to as Visual Space--the linear, quantitative mode of perception that is characteristic of the Western world; on the other hand there is Acoustic Space--the holistic, qualitative reasoning of the East. The medium of print, the authors argue, fosters and preserves the perception of Visual Space; but, like television, the technologies of the data base, the communications satellite, and the global media network are pushing their users towards the more dynamic, &quot;many-centered&quot; orientation of Acoustic Space.  The authors warn, however, that this movement towards Acoustic Space may not go smoothly. Indeed, McLuhan and Powers argue that with the advent of the global village--the result of worldwide communications--these two worldviews &quot;are slamming into each other at the speed of light,&quot; asserting that &quot;the key to peace is to understand both these systems simultaneously.&quot;  Employing McLuhan\'s concept of the Tetrad--a device for predicting the changes wrought by new technologies--the authors analyze this collision of viewpoints. Taking no sides, they seek to do today what McLuhan did so successfully twenty-five years ago--to look around the corner of the coming world, and to help us all be prepared for what we will find there.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"3463483825302577122\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer       var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_27311758'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27311758-the-great-acceleration?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Great Acceleration: An Environmental History of the Anthropocene Since 1945<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/68730.John_Robert_McNeill?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">John Robert McNeill<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.69 avg rating &mdash; 108 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2016\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer14784135228485987213\">The Earth has entered a new age--the Anthropocene--in which humans are the most powerful influence on global ecology. Since the mid-twentieth century, the accelerating pace of energy use, greenhouse gas emissions, and population growth has thrust the<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText14784135228485987213\" style=\"display:none\">The Earth has entered a new age--the Anthropocene--in which humans are the most powerful influence on global ecology. Since the mid-twentieth century, the accelerating pace of energy use, greenhouse gas emissions, and population growth has thrust the planet into a massive uncontrolled experiment. The Great Acceleration explains its causes and consequences, highlighting the role of energy systems, as well as trends in climate change, urbanization, and environmentalism.\n\nMore than any other factor, human dependence on fossil fuels inaugurated the Anthropocene. Before 1700, people used little in the way of fossil fuels, but over the next two hundred years coal became the most important energy source. When oil entered the picture, coal and oil soon accounted for seventy-five percent of human energy use. This allowed far more economic activity and produced a higher standard of living than people had ever known--but it created far more ecological disruption.\n\nWe are now living in the Anthropocene. The period from 1945 to the present represents the most anomalous period in the history of humanity\'s relationship with the biosphere. Three-quarters of the carbon dioxide humans have contributed to the atmosphere has accumulated since World War II ended, and the number of people on Earth has nearly tripled. So far, humans have dramatically altered the planet\'s biogeochemical systems without consciously managing them. If we try to control these systems through geoengineering, we will inaugurate another stage of the Anthropocene. Enveloped by mystery whether he reached Mount Everest\'s summit before <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2324822616746653569\" style=\"display:none\">\'Climbing Everest is all about heart.\' - George Leigh Mallory\n\nGeorge Leigh Mallory was both the first modern climber and the last towering figure of the Great Age of Exploration. Enveloped by mystery whether he reached Mount Everest\'s summit before his fall, he continues to grip the imagination. An exceptionally gifted and driven climber, his spell-binding memory inspires mountaineers to this day, attracting lively speculation as well as fact-finding expeditions to retrace his steps. Climbing Everest gathers for the first time Mallory\'s influential canon on mountaineering from its disparate locations in archives.\n\nMallory was unique in drawing a new literature from his mountain craft. For him, as for his predecessors, earth was still a heroic place with hidden parts promising novel experiences while the eyes of history were trained upon them. But he was strongly inspired by the Bloomsbury group, unlike previous explorers, and a talented writer and poet. He chose to break with the Edwardian stiff upper lip in favor of emotional truthfulness about the art of climbing. The result created a novel branch of mountaineering literature, as fresh and vivid as the feelings he recorded in handwriting under the most harrowingly extreme mountain-top conditions.\n\n--From the Stamped from the Beginning uses the lives of five major American intelle<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4236964297762095122\" style=\"display:none\">In this deeply researched and fast-moving narrative, Kendi chronicles the entire story of anti–Black racist ideas and their staggering power over the course of American history. Stamped from the Beginning uses the lives of five major American intellectuals to offer a window into the contentious debates between assimilationists and segregationists and between racists and anti-racists. From Puritan minister Cotton Mather to Thomas Jefferson, from fiery abolitionist William Lloyd Garrison to brilliant scholar W. E. B. Du Bois to legendary anti–prison activist Angela Davis, Kendi shows how and why some of our leading pro-slavery and pro–civil rights thinkers have challenged or helped cement racist ideas in America.\n\nAs Kendi illustrates, racist thinking did not arise from ignorance or hatred. Racist ideas were created and popularized in an effort to defend deeply entrenched discriminatory policies and to rationalize the nation’s racial inequities in everything from wealth to health. While racist ideas are easily produced and easily consumed, they can also be discredited. In shedding much–needed light on the murky history of racist ideas, Stamped from the Beginning offers tools to expose them—and in the process, reason to hope.<\/span>\n  <a What is it about its thirty-two figurative pieces, moving about its sixty-four black and white squares according to very simple rules, that has captivated people for nearly 1,500 years? Why has it driven some of its greatest players into paranoia and madness, and yet is hailed as a remarkably powerful educational tool? Nearly everyone has played chess at some point in their lives. Its rules and pieces have served as a metaphor for society including military strategy, mathematics, artificial intelligence, literature, and the arts. It has been condemned as the devil’s game by popes, rabbis, and imams, and lauded as a guide to proper living by different popes, rabbis, and imams. In his wide-ranging and ever fascinating examination of chess, David Shenk gleefully unearths the hidden history of a game that seems so simple yet contains infinity. From its invention somewhere in India around 500 A.D., to its enthusiastic adoption by the Persians and its spread by Islamic warriors, to its remarkable use as a moral guide in the Middle Ages and its political utility in the Enlightenment, to its crucial importance in the birth of cognitive science and its key role in the new aesthetic of modernism in 20th century art, to its 21st century importance to the development of artificial intelligence and use as a teaching tool in inner-city America, chess has been a remarkably omnipresent factor in the development of civilization. Indeed as Shenk shows, some neuroscientists believe that playing chess may actually alter the structure of the brain, that it may for individuals be what it has been for civilization: a virus that It would appear that the formula: IQ+Effort=Merit may well constitute the basic belief of the ruling class in the twenty-first century. Projecting himself into the year 2034, the author of this sociological satire shows how present decisions and practices may remold our society.\n\nIt is widespread knowledge that it is insufficient to be somebody\'s nephew to obtain a responsible post in business, government, teaching, or science. Experts in education and selection apply scientific principles to sift out the leaders of tomorrow. You need intelligence rating, qualification, experience, application, and a certain caliber to achieve status. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11904381669122787473">An internationally-recognized thought leader known as the Disaster Avoidance Expert, Dr. Gleb Tsipursky is on a mission to protect leaders from dangerous judgment errors known as cognitive biases by developing the most effective decision-making strategies. <br/><br/>He wrote several best-selling books, including Never Go With Your Gut: How Pioneering Leaders Make the Best Decisions and Avoid Business Disast</span>
  <span id="freeText11904381669122787473" style="display:none">An internationally-recognized thought leader known as the Disaster Avoidance Expert, Dr. Gleb Tsipursky is on a mission to protect leaders from dangerous judgment errors known as cognitive biases by developing the most effective decision-making strategies. <br /><br />He wrote several best-selling books, including Never Go With Your Gut: How Pioneering Leaders Make the Best Decisions and Avoid Business Disasters (Career Press, 2019), The Blindspots Between Us: How to Overcome Unconscious Cognitive Bias and Build Better Relationships (New Harbinger, 2020), and Resilience: Adapt and Plan for the New Abnormal of the COVID-19 Coronavirus Pandemic (Changemakers Books, 2020). Dr. Tsipursky’s cutting-edge thought leadership was featured in over 550 articles and 450 interviews in Fast Company, CBS News, CNBC, Entrepreneur, Time, Business Insider, Government Executive, The Chronicle of Philanthropy, Inc. Magazine, and elsewhere.<br /><br />His expertise stems from over 20 years of consulting, coaching, speaking, and training experience as CEO of Disaster Avoidance Experts. Its hundreds of clients, mid-size and large companies and nonprofits, span North America, Europe, and Australia, and include Aflac, IBM, Honda, Wells Fargo, and the World Wildlife Fund. It also comes from his strong research and teaching background in behavioral economics and cognitive neuroscience with over 15 years in academia, including 7 years as a professor at the Ohio State University. He published dozens of peer-reviewed articles in academic journals such as Behavior and Social Issues and Journal of Social and Political Psychology.<br /><br />He lives in Columbus, OH, and to avoid disaster in his personal life makes sure to spend ample time with his wife. Contact him at Gleb[at]DisasterAvoidanceExperts[dot]com, follow him on Twitter @gleb_tsipursky, Instagram @dr_gleb_tsipursky, and register for his free Wise Decision Maker Course <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://disasteravoidanceexperts.com/subscribe/">https://disasteravoidanceexperts.com/...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11904381669122787473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
